Duration of Breastfeeding for Legal Prohibition: Hanafi vs Majority
Dispute on the duration of breastfeeding that establishes legal kinship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi (majority) and Abu Hanifa's positions on the duration of breastfeeding that creates marriage prohibition, and evaluate the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Majority: two years; Abu Hanifa: two years plus six months for weaning effect.

This passage addresses a key ikhtilaf in family law: the timeframe in which breastfeeding establishes legal kinship (ḥurmat al-riḍāʿ). Understanding the duration and the reasoning behind each position is essential for correctly applying rulings on marriage prohibitions. The majority relies on explicit Quranic verses and a hadith, while Imam Abu Hanifa introduces a six‑month extension based on the infant's dietary needs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi (majority) position
Identify which view is attributed to Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and the other three imams. Note that this is the relied‑upon position within the Hanafi school (mufta bih).
The majority holds two complete years (ḥawlān kāmilān).
2
Identify the opponent and their dalīl
Recognize that Abu Hanifa is the opposing voice within the Hanafi school. His evidence is based on the need to change the infant's diet after two years.
Abu Hanifa adds six months, totalling two and a half years.
3
Follow the majority's proof
Analyze the Quranic verses (2:233, 46:15) and the hadith from al‑Daraquṭnī. Understand how they support the two‑year limit.
The thirty‑month rule minus six months pregnancy yields twenty‑four months of breastfeeding.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa's argument is that the verses are not explicit cutoffs; the need for complete weaning justifies an extension. Evaluate why the majority considers his proof weak.
The text in Fath al‑Qadir describes his evidence as 'all weak'.
5
Determine the thamarah al‑khilāf
Identify the practical consequence: if a child is breastfed after two years, does it create a marriage prohibition?
According to the majority: no. According to Abu Hanifa: yes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عند غيره فمدته حولان (1) ٢٠٥ [ ۱ ] قوله : وأما عند غيره ... الخ ؛ ذهب أبو يوسف له ومحمد له وغيرهما من الأئمة الثلاثة إلى أن مدة الرضاع التي يثبت فيها أحكام الرضاعة حولان ؛ لقوله : وَالْوَالِدَاتُ يُرْضِعْنَ أَوْلَدَهُنَّ حَوْلَيْنِ كَامِلَيْنِ لِمَنْ أَرَادَ أَن يُتِمَّ الرَّضَاعَةَ ) ، وقوله حالة : وَحَمْلُهُ وَفِصَالُهُ ثَلَثُونَ شَهْراً (۳) ، بناءً على أن أقل مدة الحمل ستة أشهر، والباقي مدة الرضاع. وأخرج الدارقطني مرفوعاً: «لا رضاعَ إلا في حولين»، وفي الباب أخبار وآثار كثيرة تدلّ عليه. وأما أبو حنيفة له فاستدلوا لإثبات مذهبه بوجوه كلها ضعيفة على ما بسطه في «فتح القدير» وغيره : ١. منها : إنه لا بد من تغيير الغذاء للرضيع المتعود باللبن في الحولين ؛ لينقطع الإنبات باللبن، وذلك بزيادة مدّة يتعوّد الصبي فيها غيره، فقدرناها بستة أشهر ؛ لكون هذه المدة أقل مدة الحمل. (۱) اختلف الفقهاء في مدة الرضاع : فقال زفر ما دام يجتزئ باللبن ولم يفطم فهو رضاع، وإن أتى عليه ثلاث سنين. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد والثوري والحسن بن صالح والشافعي : يحرم في الحولين ولا يحرم بعدهما، ولا يعتبر الفطام وإنما يعتبر الوقت . وقال ابن وهب عن مالك : قليل الرضاع وكثيره محرم في الحولين، وما كان بعد الحولين فإنه لا يحرم قليله ولا كثيره. وقال ابن القاسم عن مالك : الرضاع حولان وشهر أو شهران بعد ذلك، ولا ينظر إلى إرضاع أمه إياه إنما ينظر إلى الحولين وشهر أو شهرين. وقال الأوزاعي : إذا فطم لسنة واستمر فطامه فليس بعده رضاع، ولو أرضع ثلاث سنين لم يفطم لم يكن رضاعاً بعد الحولين. ينظر : (الأم) (٥)) (۲۹)، و«المدونة»(۲ : ۲۹۸)، و«أحكام القرآن للجصاص (۱) : (٥٦١) ، و (طرح التثريب (۷): ۱۳۸)، و(حاشية العدوي» (۲ : ۱۲۸)، و(منح العلي (۲) : (۸۸)، و(حاشية البيجرمي (٤) : (۷۳)، و(الموسوعة الفقهية الكويتية (٢٢: ٢٤٧). As for other than him, its duration is two years. (1) 205 [1] His statement: "As for other than him...etc.": Abu Yusuf (may Allah be pleased with him), Muhammad (may Allah be pleased with him), and others among the three imams held that the duration of breastfeeding in which the rules of breastfeeding are established is two years, due to His statement: "Mothers shall nurse their children for two complete years for those who wish to complete the nursing" (Quran 2:233), and His statement: "And his gestation and weaning are thirty months" (Quran 46:15), based on the fact that the minimum duration of pregnancy is six months, and the remainder is the duration of breastfeeding. Al-Daraqutni narrated it as marfu': "No breastfeeding except within two years." And in this chapter there are many reports and traditions indicating it. As for Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him), they adduced to establish his school several objections, all weak, as detailed in Fath al-Qadir and others: 1. Among them: it is necessary to change the food for the infant accustomed to milk within the two years to stop the growth by milk, so we estimated it as six months because this duration is the minimum period of pregnancy. (1) The jurists differed about the duration of breastfeeding: Zufar said: as long as it suffices with milk and is not weaned, it is breastfeeding, even if three years pass. Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, al-Thawri, al-Hasan ibn Salih, and al-Shafi'i said: it prohibits within two years and does not prohibit after them, and weaning is not considered; only the time is considered. Ibn Wahb reported from Malik: a little and much of breastfeeding is prohibited within two years, and what is after two years, neither a little nor much prohibits it. Ibn al-Qasim reported from Malik: breastfeeding is two years and a month or two months after that, and no regard is given to the mother's nursing him; only two years and a month or two months are considered. Al-Awza'i said: if weaned at one year and weaning continues, there is no breastfeeding after it; even if he nurses for three years without weaning, it is not breastfeeding after two years. See: al-Umm (5:29), al-Mudawwana (2:298), Ahkam al-Quran by al-Jassas (1:561), Tahrir al-Tathrib (7:138), Hashiyat al-Adawi (2:128), Manh al-Ali (2:88), Hashiyat al-Bijirmi (4:73), and al-Mawsu'at al-Fiqhiyya al-Kiwaytiyya (22:247). (2) Surah al-Baqara, part of verse 233. (3) Surah al-Ahqaf, part of verse 15.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the duration of breastfeeding that creates legal prohibition. The majority of scholars, including Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and the three other Sunni imams (al-Shafi'i, Malik, Ahmad), hold that the duration is two complete years (hawlayn). Their proof is the Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqara (2:233) which mentions two complete years for those who wish to complete nursing, and Surah al-Ahqaf (46:15) which states that the total period of gestation and weaning is thirty months. Since the minimum pregnancy is six months, the remaining twenty-four months (two years) is the time for weaning. Additionally, al-Daraqutni narrated a hadith: 'No breastfeeding except within two years.' Abu Hanifa, however, holds that the duration is two and a half years (two years plus six months). His reasoning is based on the need to change the infant's diet after two years; since the infant is accustomed to milk, an additional period is needed to complete the weaning process. He estimated this additional period as six months, because that is the minimum duration of pregnancy. The footnote summarizes the views of various scholars: Zufar allows up to three years if not weaned; Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, al-Thawri, al-Shafi'i strictly say two years; Malik's view varies between two years and two years plus a month or two; al-Awza'i considers weaning at one year as cutoff. The text notes that Abu Hanifa's proofs are considered weak by many.

Key Terms
حولان (ḥawlān): Two years; the duration of breastfeeding according to the majority of scholars.
أقل مدة الحمل (aqall muddat al-ḥaml): Minimum duration of pregnancy, which is six months in Hanafi fiqh.
فطام (fiṭām): Weaning; the act of stopping breastfeeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the strongest evidence for the majority view (two years) according to the passage?
A) Qiyas on the minimum pregnancy period.
B) The hadith 'No breastfeeding except within two years' narrated by al-Daraqutni.
C) The consensus of the Sahaba.
D) The need to change the infant's diet.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that breastfeeding after two complete years does not create kinship prohibition, based on explicit Quranic and hadith evidence.

The Number of Sucklings: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute over necessity of five sucklings for prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the number of sucklings required for fosterage prohibition and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
Any amount of breastfeeding, even one suck, establishes fosterage prohibition in the Hanafi school.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the minimum number of breastfeedings required to establish the prohibition of marriage (mahramiyya). The Shafi'i school requires five separate sucklings, while the Hanafi school holds that even one or two suffices. The commentator defends the Hanafi position by arguing that the five-suckling rule was also abrogated, as indicated by companion statements.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding the number of sucklings that establish fosterage prohibition.
The matn states the saying of Abu Hanifa, and the commentator affirms it as the stronger view.
2
Identify the opposing school and its view
Name the school that disagrees and its specific requirement.
The Shafi'i school requires five complete sucklings (massah).
3
Analyze the opponent's proof
Examine the dalil the Shafi'i school uses, specifically the hadith of Aisha about abrogation from ten to five.
The hadith is authentic but its interpretation is contested.
4
Trace the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school refutes the Shafi'i evidence, arguing that the five-suckling rule was itself abrogated.
The Hanafi school relies on general Quranic verses and companion statements.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of this difference in rulings.
In practice, a child nursed only once is a mahram for marriage according to Hanafis, but not according to Shafi'is.

[1]قوله : بخمس مصات ; فلا تحرم الرضعة بالمصة والمصتين، ودليله حديث عائشة رضي الله عنهم : كان فيما أنزل من القرآن عشر رضعات معلومات يحرمن، ثمّ نسخن بخمس رضعات معلومات يحرمن ، فتوفى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهن فيما يقرأ في القرآن (3) ، أخرجه مسلم. ولنا: إطلاق الآيات والأحاديث الواردة في باب تحريم الرضاع. والجواب عما استدل به : أن حكم الخمس أيضاً نسخ كحكم العشرة، وقول عائشة رضي الله عنها يدلّ على قرب النسخ من زمان الوفاة النبوية، حتى أن من لم يبلغه النسخ كان يقرؤه ، وإلا لزم ضياعُ بعض القرآن الذي لم ينسخ. ويؤيده ما روى عن ابن عباس و الله أنه قيل له : إنّ الناس يقولون : إنّ الرضعة لا تحرم ، فقال : كان ذلك ثم نسخ. وعن ابن مسعود : آل أمر الرضاع إلى أن قليله وكثيرة يحرم. وعنه له أنه قيل له ابن الزبير يقول : لا بأس بالرضعة والرضعتين ، فقال : قضاء الله خير من قضاء ابن الزبير، قال الله : وَأُمَّهَتُكُمُ الَّتِي أَرْضَعْنَكُمْ وَأَخَوَاتُكُم مِّنَ الرَّضَعَةِ (4) ، كذا حققه في «فتح القدير»).
Book of Fosterage: Its Definition and Rulings. According to al-Shafi'i, it is established by five sucklings. The matn states the saying of Abu Hanifa, and they did not mention the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) although the more correct and stronger is [Abu Hanifa's]. [1] His saying: 'By five sucklings' means that a single suck and two sucks do not establish prohibition. Its proof is the hadith of Aisha—may Allah be pleased with them—: 'Among what was revealed of the Quran were ten known sucklings that make forbidden; then they were abrogated by five known sucklings that make forbidden; then the Prophet, peace be upon him, passed away while they were recited in the Quran'—Muslim narrated it. Our evidence: the general verses and ahadith found in the chapter of fosterage prohibition. The response to what he adduced: that the ruling of five was also abrogated like the ruling of ten, and the statement of Aisha indicates the proximity of abrogation to the time of the Prophet's death, so that one who had not learned of the abrogation would recite it; otherwise, it would necessitate the loss of some Quran that was not abrogated. Supporting this is what was narrated from Ibn Abbas: he was asked, 'People say that a single suck does not prohibit.' He said, 'That was then abrogated.' And from Ibn Mas'ud: the matter of fosterage culminated in that its little and much prohibit. And from him: he was told that Ibn al-Zubayr says there is no harm in one or two sucks; he said, 'Allah's decree is better than Ibn al-Zubayr's decree. Allah said: Your mothers who nursed you and your sisters from nursing.' This is verified in Fath al-Qadir.

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the minimum number of breastfeedings required to establish the prohibition of marriage (mahramiyya). The Shafi'i school holds that five distinct sucklings are necessary, based on the hadith of Aisha that the Quran originally prescribed ten sucklings, then abrogated to five, which were being recited at the Prophet's death. The Hanafi school relies on general Quranic verses and hadith indicating that any amount of breastfeeding establishes prohibition. The commentary refutes the Shafi'i evidence by arguing that the rule of five was also abrogated, as shown by companion statements. The Hanafi position, affirmed by the commentator, is that of Abu Hanifa (and the matn), which is that even one or two sucks create prohibition. The passage also cites supporting narrations from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Mas'ud.

مصة (massah): A single suck or drawing of milk from the breast.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a legal ruling by a later revelation.

Exception of Sister's Mother in Fosterage Prohibitions
Clarifying that the mother of one's foster sister is not prohibited, unlike lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exception to the general rule of fosterage prohibitions and explain why the mother of a foster sibling is not a mahram.

Core Idea
In fosterage, the mother of your foster sibling is not your mahram because she is not your mother or father's wife.

This passage clarifies a key exception to the principle that fosterage prohibitions mirror lineage prohibitions. While the hadith states that fosterage creates the same prohibitions as blood, the mother of one's foster sister or brother remains permissible to marry. The reasoning hinges on the underlying cause ('illa) of the prohibition.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the hadith 'What is prohibited through fosterage is what is prohibited through lineage' as the foundation.
This is a mutawatir hadith narrated by Bukhari and Muslim.
2
Identify the exception
Note the exception: 'except the mother of one's sister and brother' – meaning the mother of one's foster sibling is not prohibited.
The exception is stated in the matn of al-Wiqayah.
3
Understand the reasoning
In lineage, the mother of one's sister is either one's own mother or the woman one's father had intercourse with, both prohibited. In fosterage, she is neither, so she remains a stranger.
The prohibition is not due to the sibling relationship itself.
4
Address the objection of takhsis
The objection is that this exception seems to limit the general hadith. The response is that it is not a true specification (takhsis) but a disconnected exception (munqati'), because the reason for prohibition is absent.
The hadith applies only where the same cause exists.
5
Note the special case
If the foster sibling's mother is also one's own foster mother (because he suckled from her), then she is prohibited as a foster mother, not because of the sibling relationship.
This case is covered by the general rule, not the exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيحرم منه ما يحرم من النسب إلا أمّ أُخْتِه وأخيه [1] عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية (فيحرم منه ما يحرم من النسب إلا أمّ أُخْتِهِ وأخيه) ; فإن أُمَّ الأُخْتِ والأخ من النسب، هي الأم، أو موطوءة الأب، وكل منهما حرام، ولا كذلك من الرضاع ) وفيه أيضاً : الحق أن الرضاع وإن قل يحصل به نشوء بقدره، فكان الرضاع مطلقاً مظنّة بالنسبة إلى الصغير. وقولنا قول جمهورا الصحابة ، منهم : علي وابنُ مسعود أسند الرواية منهما النسائي ، وابن عباس له وجمهور التابعين. 1 ] قوله : إلا أم أخته ... الخ ; اعترض على استثناء هذه الصور بأن الأصل في هذا الباب حديث : «يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب»، أخرجه الشيخان، وهو بإطلاقه وعمومه يشمل الكل، فتخصيص بعض الصور منه بدليل عقلي لا يجوز. والجواب عنه على ما فصَّلَه الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «شرح الكنز (3) وغيره : إنه لا تخصيص حقيقة في هذا المقام، والاستثناء في كلامهم منقطع ، وذلك لأن الحديث يوجب عموم حرمة الرضاع، حيث وجدت الحرمة لأجل النسب، وحرمة أم أخيه من النسب لا لأجل أنها أم أخيه، بل لكونها أمه أو موطوءة أبيه. ألا يرى أنها تحرم عليه، وإن لم يكن له أخ ، وكذا أخت ابنه من النسب إنما حرمت لأجل أنها بنته أو بنت امرأته بدليل حرمتها وإن لم يكن له ابن، وهذا المعنى يوجب الحرمة في الرضاع أيضاً، حتى لا يجوز له أن يتزوج بأمه ولا موطوءة أبيه ، ولا بنت امرأته، كل ذلك من الرضاع. (2) قوله : ولا كذلك من الرضاع ; فإنّ أمّ أخيه ليست بأم له، ولا موطوءة أبيه ، بل هي أجنبية عنه. فإن قلت : قد تكون أمّ أخيه الرضاعي أماً له أيضاً، بأن كان هو ارتضع منها. قلت : هذه الصورة داخلة فيما سبق، والحرمة هنا لكونها أماً رضاعيّة له، لا لكونها أمّ أخيه الرضاعي.
So is prohibited from it what is prohibited from lineage, except the mother of one's sister and brother. [1] 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah (So is prohibited from it what is prohibited from lineage, except the mother of one's sister and brother) for the mother of the sister and brother from lineage is the mother or the woman whom the father has had intercourse with, and both are prohibited, but not so from fosterage. And in it also: the truth is that fosterage, even if little, produces growth according to its measure, so fosterage absolutely is a means [of growth] for the child. And our saying is the saying of the majority of the Companions, including 'Ali and Ibn Mas'ud—al-Nasa'i narrated from them—and Ibn 'Abbas and the majority of the Followers. [1] His saying: 'except the mother of his sister... etc.' objection was raised against the exception of these cases because the foundation in this chapter is the hadith 'What is prohibited through fosterage is what is prohibited through lineage'—narrated by the two Shaykhs—and its generality and comprehensiveness includes all, so specifying some cases by rational evidence is not permissible. The response, as detailed by al-Zayla'i in 'Sharh al-Kanz' and others: that there is no real specification in this context, and the exception in their speech is disconnected (munqati'), because the hadith requires the generality of fosterage prohibition where the prohibition exists due to lineage, and the prohibition of the mother of his brother from lineage is not because she is the mother of his brother, but because she is his mother or the woman his father had intercourse with. Do you not see that she is prohibited to him even if he has no brother? Similarly, the sister of his son from lineage is prohibited only because she is his daughter or the daughter of his wife, evidenced by her prohibition even if he has no son. This meaning requires prohibition in fosterage as well, so it is not permissible for him to marry his mother nor the woman his father had intercourse with, nor the daughter of his wife, all of that from fosterage. (2) His saying: 'but not so from fosterage' because the mother of his brother is not his mother nor the woman his father had intercourse with; rather, she is a stranger to him. If you say: 'the mother of his foster brother may also be a mother to him, if he suckled from her.' I say: this case is included in what preceded, and the prohibition here is because she is a foster mother to him, not because she is the mother of his foster brother.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage explains an exception to the general rule that fosterage relations correspond to blood relations in terms of marriage prohibitions. The general rule is based on the hadith 'What is prohibited through fosterage is what is prohibited through lineage.' However, the mother of one's foster sister or brother is not prohibited because in lineage, such a woman is either one's own mother or the woman one's father has had intercourse with—both of whom are prohibited. In fosterage, the mother of one's foster sister is not one's own mother nor the wife of one's father, so she remains a stranger (ajnabiyya) and marriage to her is permissible. The commentary addresses an objection that this exception seems to limit the general hadith. The response is that the exception is not a true limitation (takhsis); rather, the hadith means that prohibitions are established for the same underlying reasons as in lineage. In lineage, the mother of one's sister is prohibited not because she is the mother of one's sister, but because she is one's own mother or father's wife. Since that reason does not exist in fosterage, there is no prohibition. The passage also clarifies that if the foster sister's mother is also the foster mother of the man himself (because he suckled from her), then she is prohibited as a foster mother, not because she is the mother of his sister.

Key Terms
أم الأخت (umm al-ukht): The mother of one's sister; in lineage, this is one's own mother, but in fosterage it is not necessarily so.
منقطع (munqati'): Disconnected; here, the exception is munqati' because it is not a true exclusion from the general rule but rather a separate category based on different reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because she is not his mahram through fosterage.
B) No, because she is like his sister's mother.
C) Yes, but only if he did not suckle from her.
D) No, because fosterage creates full prohibition.

Key Takeaway
The mother of one's foster sibling is not a mahram for marriage because the underlying cause of prohibition (being one's own mother or father's wife) is absent in fosterage.

The Disjunctive Exception: Why the Foster-Mother of Your Sibling Is Permissible
Clarifying the exception of the foster-mother of one's sibling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the foster-mother of one's sibling and explain the rationale of the disjunctive exception (istithnā’ munqaṭi‘).

Core Idea
The mother of a foster-sibling is not prohibited because her prohibition in lineage arises from a different cause (being your mother or father's wife) which does not transfer to fosterage.

The general rule in fosterage is that foster relationships mirror blood prohibitions. However, Al-Wiqayah states an exception: the mother of one's foster-sibling is permissible. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning, showing that this is not a real exception but a disjunctive one, based on the distinct cause of prohibition in lineage.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Recall the hadith: 'What is prohibited through fosterage is what is prohibited through lineage.' This establishes a general parallelism.
This hadith is authentic (muttafaq 'alayh).
2
Identify the apparent exception
The text states: 'except the mother of his sister and his brother.' On its face, this seems to carve out an exception from the general rule.
The exception covers both the foster-mother of a sister and a brother.
3
Analyze the cause of prohibition in lineage
In lineage, the mother of a sibling is prohibited not because she is a sibling's mother, but because she is either one's own mother or one's father's wife. This prohibition exists regardless of the sibling relationship.
For example, a woman is prohibited to her son even if she has no daughter.
4
Apply the same cause to fosterage
In fosterage, the mother of a foster-sibling is not necessarily one's own foster-mother or father's foster-wife. Unless she also suckled the person, she remains a stranger.
If she also suckled the person, she is already prohibited as a foster-mother, not because of the sibling relationship.
5
Understand the disjunctive exception
The exception is disjunctive (istithnā’ munqaṭi‘): the excepted cases are not truly part of the general rule because the underlying cause differs. Thus the generality of the hadith is preserved.
This is a key usul al-fiqh concept in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيحرم منه ما يحرم من النسب إلا أم أُخْتِه وأخيه) ؛ فإن أُمَّ الأُخْتِ والأخ من النسب، هي الأم، أو موطوءة الأب، وكل منهما حرام، ولا كذلك من الرضاع ( وفيه أيضاً : الحق أن الرضاع وإن قل يحصل به نشوء بقدره، فكان الرضاع مطلقاً مظنّة بالنسبة إلى الصغير. وقولنا قول جمهورا الصحابة ، منهم : علي وابنُ مسعود أسند الرواية منهما النسائي ، وابن عباس له وجمهور التابعين. اعترض على استثناء هذه الصور بأن الأصل في هذا الباب حديث : «يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب»، أخرجه الشيخان، وهو بإطلاقه وعمومه يشمل الكل، فتخصيص بعض الصور منه بدليل عقلي لا يجوز. والجواب عنه على ما فصَّلَه الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «شرح الكنز وغيره : إنه لا تخصيص حقيقة في هذا المقام، والاستثناء في كلامهم منقطع ، وذلك لأن الحديث يوجب عموم حرمة الرضاع، حيث وجدت الحرمة لأجل النسب، وحرمة أم أخيه من النسب لا لأجل أنها أم أخيه، بل لكونها أمه أو موطوءة أبيه. ألا يرى أنها تحرم عليه، وإن لم يكن له أخ ، وكذا أخت ابنه من النسب إنما حرمت لأجل أنها بنته أو بنت امرأته بدليل حرمتها وإن لم يكن له ابن، وهذا المعنى يوجب الحرمة في الرضاع أيضاً، حتى لا يجوز له أن يتزوج بأمه ولا موطوءة أبيه ، ولا بنت امرأته، كل ذلك من الرضاع. ولا كذلك من الرضاع ; فإنّ أمّ أخيه ليست بأم له، ولا موطوءة أبيه ، بل هي أجنبية عنه. فإن قلت : قد تكون أمّ أخيه الرضاعي أماً له أيضاً، بأن كان هو ارتضع منها. قلت : هذه الصورة داخلة فيما سبق، والحرمة هنا لكونها أماً رضاعيّة له، لا لكونها أمّ أخيه الرضاعي.
Thus what is prohibited through fosterage is what is prohibited through lineage, except for the mother of his sister and his brother. For the mother of the sister and brother through lineage is the mother or the father's wife, and each of them is unlawful, but not so through fosterage. And in it also: the truth is that fosterage, even if little, causes growth proportionate to it, so fosterage absolutely is a cause for the young child. And our statement is the statement of the majority of the Companions, among them: Ali and Ibn Mas'ud, al-Nasa'i narrated from them, and Ibn Abbas and the majority of the Successors. An objection was raised against the exception of these cases because the basis in this chapter is the hadith: 'What is prohibited through fosterage is what is prohibited through lineage,' narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim, and its absolute and general meaning includes everything, so specifying some cases by rational evidence is not permissible. The answer according to what al-Zayla'i detailed in Sharh al-Kanz and others is that there is no real specification in this context, and the exception in their speech is disjunctive. This is because the hadith requires the generality of the prohibition of fosterage wherever prohibition exists due to lineage, and the prohibition of the mother of his brother through lineage is not because she is the mother of his brother, but because she is his mother or his father's wife. Do you not see that she is prohibited to him even if he has no brother? Likewise, the daughter of his son through lineage is prohibited only because she is his daughter or the daughter of his wife, as evidenced by her prohibition even if he has no son. This meaning also entails prohibition in fosterage, so that he may not marry his mother, nor his father's wife, nor the daughter of his wife—all of this through fosterage. And it is not so through fosterage; for the mother of his brother is not his mother, nor his father's wife, but she is a stranger to him. If you say: The mother of his foster-brother may also be his mother if he suckled from her. I say: This case is included in what preceded, and the prohibition here is because she is his foster-mother, not because she is the mother of his foster-brother.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage addresses a key exception in the law of fosterage (رضاع). The general rule, established by the hadith 'What is prohibited through fosterage is what is prohibited through lineage,' implies that all blood relatives are also prohibited as foster relatives. However, the text of Al-Wiqayah states an exception: the mother of one's sister or brother through fosterage is not prohibited. The commentator explains that this is not a real exception but a disjunctive (منقطع) one. The mother of a sibling through lineage is prohibited for reasons other than being a sibling's mother—she is either one's own mother or one's father's wife. In fosterage, the mother of a foster-sibling is not inherently one's own foster-mother or father's foster-wife; thus she remains permissible. The same logic applies to other apparent exceptions. The passage also refutes the objection that the hadith's generality forbids such exceptions, showing that the exception is only apparent and does not violate the hadith's ruling.

Key Terms
أم الأخت (umm al-ukht): The mother of one's sister; in context, specifically the foster-mother of one's sister.
استثناء منقطع (istithnā’ munqaṭi‘): A disjunctive exception where the excepted item is not truly part of the general ruling; it appears as an exception but is actually a separate category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the foster-mother of one's brother permissible to marry despite the general hadith?
A) Because the hadith is weak
B) Because the exception in the text is disjunctive (منقطع); she is not prohibited for the same reason as in lineage
C) Because fosterage does not create any prohibitions
D) Because the Quran overrides the hadith

Key Takeaway
The foster-mother of one's sibling is permissible because her prohibition in lineage is due to a cause (being one's mother or father's wife) that is absent in fosterage; the exception is disjunctive, preserving the general rule.

The Three Scenarios of Prohibited Fosterage Relationships
Definition of three prohibited fosterage scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of prohibited fosterage relationships and apply them to determine whether a specific marriage is prohibited.

Core Idea
In fosterage, prohibition arises if at least one party is connected by radaa' – it need not be both.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah unpacks the precise situations in which a milk-relationship (radaa') creates a prohibition to marry. It answers a subtle question: does prohibition require both the mother and the sibling to be foster-connected, or only one? The answer expands the scope of prohibition beyond a literal reading of the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the first part of the passage and list the three combinations where a fosterage relationship creates a marriage prohibition.
Each scenario involves a mother (by lineage or fosterage) and a sibling (by lineage or fosterage).
2
Analyze the ambiguity
Notice the objection raised: if 'mother' and 'sister' are both taken as fosterage, the statement does not cover cases where only one is foster. What does the objector assume?
The objection assumes both terms must be interpreted consistently.
3
Understand the response
The text clarifies that the intended meaning is that either the mother or the sibling (or both) is connected by fosterage. This resolves the ambiguity.
The phrase 'أعم من أن يكون إحداهما فقط' indicates the inclusive scope.
4
Compare with lineage case
Read the last part about 'the sister of his son'. Contrast the lineage sister (daughter or stepdaughter) with the foster sister. Why is the latter not automatically prohibited?
In lineage, the daughter's mother is the man's wife; in fosterage, the mother's marital status is not tied in the same way.

Source Text

The chapter of fosterage / its definition and rulings. It includes three scenarios: 1) The mother by fosterage for a sister or brother by lineage. 2) The mother by lineage for a sister or brother by fosterage. 3) The mother by fosterage for a sister or brother by fosterage. If it is said: His statement 'except the mother of his sister' - if by 'mother' is meant the foster mother and by 'sister' the foster sister, then it does not include the case where only one of them is by fosterage. And if by 'mother' is meant the lineage mother and by 'sister' the foster sister, or vice versa, it does not include the other two scenarios. We say: The intent is that one of them is by fosterage, regardless of whether it is only one or both. And the sister of his son; because the lineage sister of one's son is either his daughter or his stepdaughter, and either of them has had her mother intercourse (with the man), but not so in the case of fosterage.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a definition-ruling on the types of mahram relationships through radaa' (fosterage). The author begins by stating that the subject covers three scenarios regarding who is prohibited to marry. The first scenario: a woman who is your foster mother (she breastfed you) is prohibited to you in relation to your lineage sister or brother (i.e., you cannot marry your foster mother just because she is the mother of your lineage sibling). The second scenario: your lineage mother is prohibited in relation to your foster sister or brother (i.e., your own mother is prohibited for your foster sibling's lineage). The third scenario: a foster mother is prohibited in relation to a foster sister or brother (i.e., two people who are both connected to you through fosterage are prohibited). A question then arises: the phrase 'except the mother of his sister' seems ambiguous because if both 'mother' and 'sister' are taken as foster relations, it excludes cases where only one is by fosterage. The answer clarifies that the intended meaning is that at least one of the two relations (the mother or the sister) is by fosterage; it can be just one or both. Then the text discusses the sister of one's son: a lineage sister of a son is either the man's own daughter (by his wife) or his stepdaughter (from a previous marriage), and in both cases her mother has been sexually penetrated (by the man), making her automatically prohibited. However, in fosterage, this automatic prohibition does not apply because the mother's marital relationship is not established in the same way.

Key Terms
رضاع (raḍāʿ): The act of a woman breastfeeding a child, which establishes a milk-relationship (radaa') that creates legal prohibitions.
أم نسباً (umm nasaban): A woman who is one's mother by birth (lineage).
أم رضاعاً (umm raḍāʿan): A woman who breastfed one, becoming a foster mother.
أخت نسباً (ukht nasaban): A sister by birth (lineage).
أخت رضاعاً (ukht raḍāʿan): A sister through being breastfed by the same woman.
ربيبة (rabībah): Stepdaughter (daughter of one's wife from a previous marriage).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the three scenarios of prohibited fosterage relationships according to the passage?
A) Only when both mother and sibling are by fosterage.
B) When the mother is by fosterage and the sibling by lineage, or vice versa, or both by fosterage.
C) Only when the mother is by lineage and the sibling by fosterage.
D) Only when the mother is by fosterage and the sibling by lineage.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a marriage prohibition through fosterage exists if at least one of the two individuals (mother or sibling) is connected by fosterage, not necessarily both.

The Scope of Fosterage Prohibitions in Extended Family
Explaining the application of fosterage prohibitions to relatives beyond immediate family

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which extended family members are made mahram through fosterage and distinguish between permissible and prohibited relationships using the three-form analysis.

Core Idea
Fosterage creates mahram only in the direct line; aunts and grandmothers are not made mahram.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the application of fosterage (rada') prohibitions to relatives beyond the immediate family. The commentator expands on a list from the matn, explaining that the prohibition only applies through specific relationships. Understanding this scope is crucial for correctly determining who is permissible to marry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, identify the specific relative being discussed (e.g., grandmother of son, mother of uncle) and determine whether the passage declares marriage to them as halal or haram.
The default ruling for marriage is mubah; prohibition requires a clear dalil.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Quranic verse (4:22) cited as evidence for prohibition of the entered woman of a grandfather, which then extends to mothers of uncles and aunts by lineage.
The verse is qat'i both in transmission and meaning.
3
Apply the three-form analysis
For each relative, consider the three possibilities: both the connecting relative and the person are through fosterage, one is foster and the other lineage, or vice versa. Only when the connecting link is through lineage does prohibition apply.
The key is the connecting link (the 'mother' in 'mother of brother').
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Contrast the Hanafi restrictive approach with the Shafi'i position that extends fosterage prohibitions to all relatives that would be prohibited by lineage.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi ruling is that fosterage does not create mahram beyond the direct line (mother, daughter, sister). All extended relatives (aunts, grandmothers) remain permissible unless they fall under the prohibition of 'what fathers married' through lineage.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah as confirmed in al-Bahr.

Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, clarifying the application of fosterage (rada') prohibitions to extended family members. The passage type is a ruling with proof, where the commentator expands on the original matn's list of relatives whose marital relations are affected by fosterage.

The author first addresses the sister of one's son. He explains that if both the son's sister and the connecting relative (e.g., the mother) are related only by fosterage, or one is by lineage and the other by fosterage, the prohibition does not apply in all cases. The key principle is that for fosterage to create a prohibition, the foster relationship must exist in the connecting link (the person who bridges the two individuals). So, if a man's wife is the foster-mother of his son's sister, that does not make the sister forbidden to him unless the wife is also the biological mother of that sister by lineage. The commentator states that the intended meaning is that only one of the two (the mother or the sister) is through fosterage, which covers three possibilities: both are foster, the mother is foster and the sister is lineage, or the sister is foster and the mother is lineage. But the last two only apply if the connecting link is the foster relationship.

Then he discusses the grandmother of one's son. This grandmother can be either the son's biological grandmother (his mother or his mother's mother) or his foster grandmother. If she is a foster grandmother, she is not a mahram (unmarriageable kin) because the foster relationship does not extend to such distant relatives. All such grandmothers are permissible to marry because they are unrelated (ajnabiyyat) to the man.

Next, the mothers of paternal uncle, paternal aunt, maternal uncle, and maternal aunt. The commentator notes that these mothers, by lineage, are either the entered woman of the true grandfather (father's father) or the invalid grandfather (mother's father). The entered woman of any grandfather is forbidden (mahram) based on the Quranic verse 'Do not marry what your fathers married' (4:22). However, if the relationship is through fosterage, these women are not forbidden because fosterage does not create such extended prohibitions.

The commentator repeatedly reminds the reader to apply the 'three forms' (both foster, one foster one lineage, or the reverse) to all these cases. The underlying legal principle is that fosterage creates the same prohibitions as lineage only in the direct line (mother, daughter, sister, etc.) and does not extend to more remote relations like aunts and grandmothers. The proof cited is the Quranic verse and the consensus of the Hanafi school.

Overall, this passage sharpens the student's understanding of how fosterage prohibitions are limited and do not create blanket prohibitions across all relatives. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that the three possible combinations must be considered, and only when both the connecting relative and the person in question are linked by fosterage does the prohibition apply. Otherwise, the marriage is permissible.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): Fosterage: the relationship established when a child is breastfed by a woman other than his biological mother under certain conditions, creating legal prohibitions similar to lineage.
نسب (nasab): Lineage: biological relationship through birth.
ربيبة (rabibah): Step-daughter: daughter of one's wife from a previous marriage. She is forbidden to marry if her mother has been consummated with.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, which of the following women is permissible (halal) for a man to marry?
A) The mother of his paternal uncle, if the uncle is related by lineage.
B) The grandmother of his son, if the grandmother is a foster-grandmother through his wife.
C) His step-daughter whose mother he has not consummated with.
D) The mother of his maternal aunt, if the aunt is related by lineage.

Key Takeaway
Fosterage in the Hanafi school only creates marriage prohibitions in the direct line; extended relatives like aunts and grandmothers remain permissible unless they are prohibited through lineage.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Fosterage and Extended Relatives: Grandmother of Son and Mother of Uncle
Explains that fosterage does not prohibit these relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying the grandmother of one's son through fosterage and apply the principle that fosterage mirrors lineage only in specific mahram relationships.

Core Idea
Fosterage creates prohibitions only for lineage mahram; extended relatives like son's grandmother remain permissible.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies that a man may marry his son's foster grandmother, his uncle's foster mother, and similar relatives by fosterage. The Hanafi school restricts fosterage prohibitions to the same relatives who are mahram by lineage. Understanding this distinction prevents unnecessary restrictions and preserves the original permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key relatives discussed
The passage discusses the grandmother of the son, the mother of the paternal uncle, the mother of the maternal uncle, etc. Note that these are not immediate mahram like mother or sister.
These are 'extended' relatives who are mahram only through lineage (e.g., son's grandmother is the mother of the son's wife, not directly related to the man).
2
Distinguish lineage vs. fosterage for each
The commentary states that the prohibition from lineage (because of the Quranic verse) does not extend to fosterage. For example, the grandmother of the son is only prohibited if she is related by lineage; if the relationship is through fosterage, she is permissible.
The key is whether the relationship is one that would be prohibited by lineage. If yes, then fosterage also prohibits; if no, fosterage does not prohibit.
3
Analyze the three scenarios
The commentary mentions three possible scenarios: both persons are related by fosterage, one by lineage and the other by fosterage, or vice versa. In all these cases, no prohibition exists unless the link through lineage is present.
This step helps understand that the ruling is consistent regardless of how the foster relationship mixes with lineage.
4
Apply the Quranic verse (An-Nisa 4:22)
The prohibition 'Do not marry what your fathers have married' applies only to lineage fathers (true or faulty grandfathers). Since fosterage does not create a 'father' relationship in the literal sense, the verse does not extend to foster grandmothers or similar.
The Hanafi interpretation restricts the verse's application to lineage relationships only.
5
Understand the Hanafi restriction on fosterage
The Hanafi school holds that fosterage establishes prohibition only for the same relatives who are mahram by lineage (mother, daughter, sister, etc.). Relatives beyond these—like son's grandmother or uncle's mother—are not included, making them permissible to marry.
This contrasts with the Shafi'i school which extends fosterage prohibitions to all lineage relationships.

كتاب الرضاع / تعريفه وأحكامه
وجدة ابنه ، وأُم عمه، وعمته ، وخاله، وخالته
( وجدة ابنه ) : جدة الابن نسباً إما أُمه أو أم موطوءته، ولا كذلك من الرضاع.
(وأم عمه، وعمته وخاله ، وخالته)، اعلم أنَّ أمَّ هؤلاء" نسباً إِمَّا موطوءة الجد الصحيح ، أو الجد الفاسد، ولا كذلك من الرضاع"، ولا تنس الصور الثلاث في جميع ما ذكرنا .
[١] قوله : وجدة ابنه ؛ سواءً كانت جدّة رضاعيّة للابن النسبي، أو جدة نسبية للابن الرضاعي، أو جدة رضاعيّة للابن الرضاعي، والمراد بها الجدة من قبل الأب أو الأم، فكل منهنّ حلال ؛ لكونها أجنبيات بالنسبة إليه.
(٢) قوله : وأم عمه ؛ أعم من أن يكون كلّ منهما رضاعاً أو أحدها نسباً، والآخر رضاعاً، وكذا تحل عمه ولده ، وبنت عمة ولده، وبنت أخت ولده، وأم أولاد أولاده.
[٣] قوله : هؤلاء ؛ أي العم والعمة، والخال والخالة.
[٤] قوله : أما موطوءة الجد الصحيح ؛ أي أب الأب، فإنّ العم والعمة من أولادِ الجد، فأمهم موطوءته.
[٥] قوله : أو الجد الفاسد ؛ أي أب الأم ؛ فإنّ الخال والخالة من أولاد أب الأم، فأمهم موطوءته، وأمّ موطوءة الجد صحيحاً كان أو فاسداً حرام بدلالة قوله : {وَلَا تَنكِحُوا مَا نَكَحَ وَابَاؤُكُم} (النساء: 22).
[٦] قوله : ولا كذلك من الرضاع؛ فإنّه إذا أخذ في الصور المذكورة أحدهما رضاعاً أو كلّ منهما رضاعاً لا يوجد ما يحرم.
[۷] قوله : في جميع ما ذكرنا ؛ يعني جميع الصور المذكورة تجري فيه الصور الثلاث التي ذكرها في بحث أمّ الأخ والأخت وهي أن يكون كل من المضاف إليه والمضاف رضاعاً، أو المضاف رضاعاً، والمضاف إليه نسباً، أو بالعكس.
Book of Fosterage / Its Definition and Rulings
And the grandmother of his son, and the mother of his paternal uncle, and his maternal uncle, and his maternal aunt.
(And the grandmother of his son): The grandmother of the son by lineage, either his mother or the mother of his wife, and not so from fosterage.
(And the mother of his paternal uncle, and his maternal uncle, and his maternal aunt): Know that the mother of these by lineage is either the wife of the true grandfather or the faulty grandfather, and not so from fosterage. And do not forget the three scenarios in all that we have mentioned.
[1] His saying: 'And the grandmother of his son' means whether she is a foster grandmother of the lineage son, or a lineage grandmother of the foster son, or a foster grandmother of the foster son. And what is meant is the grandmother from the father's side or the mother's side; all of them are permissible because they are alien women relative to him.
[2] His saying: 'And the mother of his paternal uncle' is more general than that both of them be fosterage, or one be lineage and the other fosterage. Likewise permissible are the paternal aunt of his child, the daughter of the paternal aunt of his child, the daughter of the sister of his child, and the mother of the children of his children.
[3] His saying: 'these' means the paternal uncle, paternal aunt, maternal uncle, and maternal aunt.
[4] His saying: 'the wife of the true grandfather' means the father's father; for the paternal uncle and aunt are among the children of the grandfather, so their mother is his wife.
[5] His saying: 'or the faulty grandfather' means the mother's father; for the maternal uncle and aunt are among the children of the mother's father, so their mother is his wife. And the wife of the grandfather, whether true or faulty, is forbidden by the indication of His saying: {And do not marry what your fathers have married} (An-Nisa: 22).
[6] His saying: 'and not so from fosterage' means that if in the mentioned scenarios one of them is fosterage or both are fosterage, there is nothing that becomes forbidden.
[7] His saying: 'in all that we have mentioned' means that all the mentioned scenarios run through the three scenarios that he mentioned in the discussion of the mother of the brother and sister: that both the addressee and the addressed be fosterage; or the addressed be fosterage and the addressee be lineage; or vice versa.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from the matn regarding who is prohibited for marriage through fosterage. The author clarifies that a man's son's grandmother (i.e., the mother of his son or the mother of his son's wife) is prohibited if she is related by lineage, but not if the relationship is through fosterage. Similarly, the mother of his paternal uncle, the mother of his maternal uncle, etc., are only prohibited if they are related by lineage. The commentary expands by stating that there are three possible scenarios: both parties are related by fosterage, one by lineage and the other by fosterage, or vice versa. The proof is the Quranic verse prohibiting marriage to one's father's wives (4:22), which applies to lineage but not fosterage because fosterage creates a prohibition only among specific relatives as stated in Hadith. The Hanafi position is that fosterage establishes prohibition only for those who would be prohibited by lineage, but the relationships mentioned here—like the grandmother of the son—are not among those. Hence they are permissible (halal).

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): Fosterage: milk-suckling relationship that creates certain marital prohibitions analogous to lineage.
جد صحيح (jadd sahih): True grandfather: father's father (agnatic grandfather).
جد فاسد (jadd fasid): Faulty grandfather: mother's father (cognatic grandfather).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man's son has a foster grandmother (through rada'), is it permissible for the man to marry her?
A) No, because she is like his own mother by fosterage.
B) Yes, because fosterage does not create prohibition in this relationship.
C) No, because the Quran prohibits marrying the wives of one's fathers.
D) Yes, because she is an alien woman (ajnabiyyah).

Key Takeaway
Fosterage prohibitions in Hanafi are limited to those who are mahram by lineage; extended relatives like son's grandmother remain permissible.

Exception to Fosterage Prohibition: Son's Sister and Grandmother
States that certain relatives are exempt from fosterage prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three exceptions to the fosterage prohibition and explain why each is halal in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, three relatives are exempt from fosterage prohibition: mother of ascendants' children, son's sister, and grandmother.

The general rule is that fosterage prohibits what lineage prohibits. However, the Hanafi school recognizes three exceptions where a relationship that would be haram by lineage remains halal by fosterage. This lesson unpacks these exceptions, their textual basis, and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
Recall the general rule: 'Yahrumu min al-rida'i ma yahrumu min al-nasab' – fosterage prohibition mirrors lineage prohibition. This is the baseline.
The matn in the passage states this principle: 'So what is prohibited from fosterage is what is prohibited from lineage'.
2
Locate the exception clause
The passage then quotes an exception: 'except the mother of the children of his ascendants, the sister of his son, and his grandmother.' Identify these three as exemptions.
The exception is from 'Al-Mukhtasar' and is the focus of the commentary.
3
Analyze each exception
For each of the three, note why they would be haram by lineage and why that cause (illa) is absent in fosterage. For example, the sister of the son is the man's daughter by lineage, but in fosterage she is not his daughter.
The commentary explains that the cause of prohibition (being a direct blood relative) does not exist.
4
Understand the reciprocity argument
The passage notes redundancy: if the mother of a man's brother is not prohibited, then the brother of a woman's son is also not prohibited. This shows the logical symmetry.
This clarifies that the exception applies reciprocally.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not recognize these exceptions; they apply the general rule strictly. Understand the Hanafi proof and the difference in practice.
The Hanafi reliance on absence of the cause (illa) is key.

Source Text

للرجل) : أي هذه النِّساء المذكورة لا تحرم للرّجل إذا كانت من الرضاع. (وأخا ابن المرأة لها رضاعاً ) : أي لا يحرم" أخو ابن المرأة لها إن كان من الرضاع واعلم أن هذا مكرّر ؛ لأنه ذكر أم الأخ، ولما كانت المرأة أم أخ الرجل، كان الرَّجلُ أخا ابن تلك المرأة.
وعبارة «المختصر » كانت كذلك : فيحرم منه ما يحرم من النسب إلا أم أولادِ أصوله، وأخت ابنه ، وجدته
[0] قوله : إذا كانت من الرضاع؛ ظاهره تعلق الرضاع بالمضاف فقط، وهو خلاف ما ذكره سابقاً من الصور الثلاث في جميع الصور، والحق أن المراد به كون قرابتهم من الرضاع، سواء تَعَلَّقَ بالمضاف أو المضاف إليه.
[٢] قوله : رضاعاً ؛ قيد لكل من الصور المذكورة على النحو الذي مرّ ذكره.
[٣) قوله : أي لا يحرم ... الخ ؛ يعني إذا كان لامرأة ابن نسباً وله آخر رضاعاً لا يحرم ذلك الأخ لها، وكذا الأخ النسبي للابن الرضاعي، وكذا الأخ الرضاعي للابن الرضاعي، وكذا يجوز للمرأة أن تتزوج بأبي أخيها وبأخي ابنها، وبأبي حفيدتها، وبجد ولدها، وبخال ولدها من الرضاع، ولا يجوز ذلك كله من النسب. كذا في «التبيين»

[٥] قوله : وجدته ؛ أي جدة ابنه، قال البرجندي: ثم إن كلاً من المذكورات يحتمل ثلاث صور، ولا يخفى أنه لا يمكنُ إرادة الصور الثلاث معاً من هذه العبارة ، وإنما غير المصنف له هذه العبارة ؛ لأنه لا يفهم منها حكم زوج الرضيع وزوجتها ، فإن حرمتهما بالمصاهرة لا بالنسب.
وأيضاً لا حاجة إلى الاستثناء ؛ لأنّ ما هو جهة الحرمة في النسب في الصور المذكورة غير موجودة في الرضاع ، مثلاً : أخت الابن إنّما يحرم من النسب؛ لكونه بنتاً
(For the man): i.e., these aforementioned women are not prohibited for the man if they are from fosterage. (And the brother of the woman's son for her through fosterage): i.e., the brother of the woman's son is not prohibited for her if he is from fosterage. Know that this is redundant because he mentioned the mother of the brother, and since the woman is the mother of the man's brother, the man is the brother of the woman's son.
And the wording of 'Al-Mukhtasar' was as follows: 'So what is prohibited from [fosterage] is what is prohibited from lineage, except the mother of the children of his ascendants, and the sister of his son, and his grandmother.'
[1] His saying: 'if they are from fosterage' – its apparent meaning is that the fosterage is attached to the addressee only, which contradicts what he mentioned earlier about the three scenarios in all cases. The truth is that what is meant is that their kinship is from fosterage, whether it relates to the addressee or the addressed.
[2] His saying: 'through fosterage' is a qualification for each of the mentioned scenarios in the manner previously mentioned.
[3] His saying: 'i.e., not prohibited...' means: if a woman has a son by lineage and another son by fosterage, that [foster] brother is not prohibited for her, likewise the lineage brother of the foster son, and likewise the foster brother of the foster son. Also it is permissible for a woman to marry the father of her brother, the brother of her son, the father of her granddaughter, the grandfather of her child, and the maternal uncle of her child from fosterage; all of that is not permitted from lineage. As in 'Al-Tabyin'.
[4] His saying: 'And know that this' – i.e., his saying 'and the brother of the woman's son' – is an objection against the author that he did not need to mention this scenario after mentioning the non-prohibition of the mother of his brother. For when it is established that the mother of a man's brother by fosterage is not prohibited for him, it is established that the brother of the woman's son is not prohibited for her, because prohibition and permissibility are reciprocal from both sides.
[5] His saying: 'and his grandmother' i.e., the grandmother of his son. Al-Burjandi said: Then each of the mentioned [exceptions] can have three scenarios, and it is not hidden that it is not possible to intend all three scenarios from this expression. Rather, the author changed this expression because one cannot understand from it the ruling of the foster child's spouse and her spouse, for their prohibition is through affinity (musahara) not lineage.
Also, there is no need for the exception because what is the cause of prohibition in lineage in the mentioned scenarios does not exist in fosterage. For example: the sister of a son is only prohibited from lineage because she is his daughter [in-law?]
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on fosterage rulings. It clarifies that the women mentioned in the previous lesson are not prohibited for a man if the relationship is through fosterage. Then it quotes from 'Al-Mukhtasar' (the matn) stating the general principle: 'What is prohibited through fosterage is what is prohibited through lineage, except the mother of the children of his ascendants, the sister of his son, and his grandmother.' This is an exception to the analogy between fosterage and lineage. The commentary explains the redundancy of the author mentioning 'the brother of the woman's son' after already stating that the mother of a man's brother is not prohibited; the relationship is reciprocal. It also notes that the exception in the matn is meant to exclude these three: (1) the mother of the children of his ascendants, i.e., the mother of his father's or mother's children (like a step-grandmother), (2) the sister of his son, and (3) his grandmother. These are halal in fosterage even though they are haram in lineage. The commentator also quotes Al-Burjandi explaining that the exception is necessary because the cause of prohibition in lineage (being a daughter or sister by birth) does not exist in fosterage for these cases. The Hanafi position is that fosterage prohibition is limited to the same categories as lineage, but with these exceptions. The proof is derived from the general principle of fosterage established by the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the absence of a specific text making these prohibited.

Key Terms
أم أولاد أصوله (umm awlad usulihi): The mother of the children of his ascendants: e.g., the wife of his father's father (step-grandmother) or the wife of his mother's father.
أخت ابنه (ukht ibnihi): The sister of his son: his son's sister (could be his daughter or step-daughter). By lineage, she is his daughter or step-daughter, hence haram. By fosterage, she is not his daughter, so halal.
جدته (jaddatuhu): His grandmother: the mother of his father or mother. By lineage, she is mahram; by fosterage, she is not.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The foster mother herself
B) The mother of the children of his ascendants
C) The foster sister
D) The foster daughter

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts three relatives from fosterage prohibition: mother of ascendants' children, son's sister, and grandmother, because the cause of prohibition in lineage is absent in fosterage.

The Three Exceptions to Prohibition by Breastfeeding (Rada') in the Hanafi School
Explaining three exemptions to rada' prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of relatives exempted from marriage prohibition by breastfeeding according to the Hanafi school, and explain the legal reasoning (illa) behind each exception.

Core Idea
Three relatives are not prohibited by breastfeeding: the mother of your ascendants' children, your son's sister, and your son's grandmother.

Islamic law generally holds that breastfeeding (rada') creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood lineage. However, the Hanafi school identifies three specific exceptions. This lesson unpacks these exceptions from the text of 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, clarifying the legal reasoning and resolving apparent redundancies in the matn.

Guided Path
1
Recall the general rule of rada'
The fundamental principle: a woman who breastfeeds a child becomes that child's mother, and her other children become siblings by breastfeeding. Thus, anyone who would be a mahram (prohibited marriage partner) by lineage becomes mahram by rada' as well. This is the baseline from which exceptions are carved.
2
Identify the three exceptions from the matn
The passage quotes al-Mukhtasar: 'It is prohibited from it that which is prohibited from lineage, except the mother of the children of his ascendants, the sister of his son, and his grandmother.' These three categories remain permissible to marry even when a breastfeeding relationship exists.
Arabic: أم أولاد أصوله، أخت ابنه، جدته
3
Understand the commentary's clarification on the phrase 'if they are from breastfeeding'
The commentary emphasizes that the phrase means the kinship itself is through breastfeeding, not that the milk is physically attached to the person. This avoids the mistaken reading that only the directly breastfed child is affected.
The author notes that the original expression in the matn could be misinterpreted; the correct understanding is that the entire relationship (such as 'sister of his son') is considered a rada' relationship.
4
Resolve the apparent redundancy regarding 'brother of the woman's son'
The commentary points out that the matn mentions 'the brother of the woman's son' after already stating that 'the mother of his brother' is not prohibited. This is actually a reciprocal application: if A is not prohibited to B, then B is not prohibited to A. The repetition reinforces the symmetry of the ruling.
This step shows the logical consistency of the exceptions: once you know the mother of a man's brother (by rada') is not prohibited to him, it follows that the brother of his son (by rada') is not prohibited to him either, because they are the same relationship seen from opposite sides.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وعبارة «المختصر » كانت كذلك : فيحرم منه ما يحرم من النسب إلا أم أولادِ أصوله، وأخت ابنه ، وجدته

[١] قوله : إذا كانت من الرضاع؛ ظاهره تعلق الرضاع بالمضاف فقط، وهو خلاف ما ذكره سابقاً من الصور الثلاث في جميع الصور، والحق أن المراد به كون قرابتهم من الرضاع، سواء تَعَلَّقَ بالمضاف أو المضاف إليه.
[٢] قوله : رضاعاً ؛ قيد لكل من الصور المذكورة على النحو الذي مرّ ذكره.
[٣) قوله : أي لا يحرم ... الخ ؛ يعني إذا كان لامرأة ابن نسباً وله آخر رضاعاً لا يحرم ذلك الأخ لها، وكذا الأخ النسبي للابن الرضاعي، وكذا الأخ الرضاعي للابن الرضاعي، وكذا يجوز للمرأة أن تتزوج بأبي أخيها وبأخي ابنها، وبأبي حفيدتها، وبجد ولدها، وبخال ولدها من الرضاع، ولا يجوز ذلك كله من النسب. كذا في «التبيين»

For the man, and the brother of the woman's son for her by breastfeeding. (For the man): i.e., these mentioned women are not prohibited for the man if they are from breastfeeding. (And the brother of the woman's son for her by breastfeeding): i.e., the brother of the woman's son is not prohibited for her if he is from breastfeeding. Know that this is repetitive because he mentioned the mother of the brother, and since the woman is the mother of the man's brother, the man is the brother of that woman's son. The expression of 'al-Mukhtasar' was thus: 'It is prohibited from it that which is prohibited from lineage, except the mother of the children of his ascendants, the sister of his son, and his grandmother.' [1] His statement: 'if they are from breastfeeding' — its apparent meaning is that the breastfeeding is attached to the first noun only, which is contrary to what he previously mentioned of the three images in all cases. The truth is that what is meant is that their kinship is through breastfeeding, whether it is attached to the first noun or the second. [2] His statement: 'by breastfeeding' — a restriction for each of the mentioned images in the manner previously mentioned. [3] His statement: 'i.e., it does not prohibit... etc.' — meaning if a woman has a biological son and another son by breastfeeding, that brother is not prohibited for her. Similarly, the biological brother of the breastfeeding son, and the breastfeeding brother of the breastfeeding son. Similarly, it is permissible for a woman to marry the father of her brother, the brother of her son, the father of her granddaughter, the grandfather of her child, and the maternal uncle of her child by breastfeeding, but all that is not permissible by lineage. Thus in 'al-Tabyeen'. [4] His statement: 'Know that this' — i.e., his statement: 'and the brother of the woman's son for him' — an objection against the author that he did not need to mention this image after mentioning the non-prohibition of the mother of his brother. For when it was established that the mother of the man's brother by breastfeeding is not prohibited to him, it is established that the brother of the woman's son is not prohibited to her, due to the reciprocity of prohibition and permissibility from both sides. [0] His statement: 'and his grandmother' — i.e., the grandmother of his son. Al-Barjandi said: Then each of the mentioned (exceptions) possibly has three images, and it is not hidden that it is not possible to intend all three images together from this expression. Rather, the author changed this expression because the ruling of the spouse of the nursing infant and his spouse is not understood from it, for their prohibition is by marriage (musaharah), not by lineage. Also there is no need for the exception, because the aspect of prohibition in lineage in the mentioned images is not present in breastfeeding. For example, the sister of the son is only prohibited by lineage because she is a daughter of the (man), thus the children of the ascendants: the brother, the sister, the paternal uncle, the paternal aunt, the maternal uncle, and the maternal aunt. So the mother of these is prohibited by lineage, not by breastfeeding.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school, explaining the exceptions to the general principle that breastfeeding establishes the same prohibitions as lineage. The core rule, stated in the matn, is that breastfeeding prohibits what lineage prohibits, except for three specific categories: the mother of the children of one's ascendants (e.g., the mother of one's brother or sister), the sister of one's son, and one's grandmother (specifically the grandmother of one's son). These are not prohibited by breastfeeding, only by lineage. The commentary clarifies that the phrase 'if they are from breastfeeding' must be understood as referring to the kinship being through breastfeeding, not merely the milk itself. It also addresses the apparent redundancy of mentioning 'brother of the woman's son' after stating that the mother of the man's brother is not prohibited, showing the symmetry of the ruling. The commentator further explains that the exceptions are limited because the legal cause (illa) for prohibition in lineage is not present in these cases in the context of rada'. For instance, the sister of one's son is prohibited by lineage because she is considered a 'daughter' by extension, but this does not apply in breastfeeding. Thus, the Hanafi position is clear: these three categories remain permissible for marriage despite a breastfeeding relationship.

Key Terms
رضاع (rada'): Breastfeeding that establishes legal kinship and prohibition on marriage.
أم أولاد الأصول (umm awlad al-usul): The mother of the children of one's ascendants (e.g., mother of one's brother or sister).
أخت ابنه (ukhtu ibnihi): The sister of one's son (by breastfeeding relationship).
جدته (jaddatuhu): His grandmother (specifically the grandmother of one's son, i.e., the mother of the son's mother or father).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT prohibited to marry despite a breastfeeding relationship?
A) A woman who breastfed the man himself
B) The sister of the man's son (by rada')
C) The mother of the man's son (by rada')
D) The maternal aunt of the man's son (by rada')

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits marriage to three specific female relatives despite a breastfeeding relationship, based on the absence of the legal cause (illa) that exists in lineage.

The Prohibition of Milk from Zina: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on milk from zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on milk from zina and explain why the prohibition applies from the mother's side but not the father's without established lineage.

Core Idea
Milk from zina prohibits marriage to the mother and her relatives, but to the father only if lineage is proven.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya discusses two key points: first, the established ruling that the husband of the wet nurse and his relatives become mahram to the nursing child, just like in lineage. Second, it dives into a debated issue: does milk produced from an extramarital pregnancy (laban al-zina) create the same marital prohibitions? The commentator presents two positions within the Hanafi school and resolves the dispute by preferring the view of al-Wabiri, which limits prohibition from the father's side. This lesson walks you through the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Recognize that the wet nurse's husband and his relatives are prohibited (mahram) to the nursing infant, analogous to blood lineage. This is the agreed-upon principle.
The base ruling is not disputed; it applies to legitimate milk.
2
Locate the disputed case
The controversy arises when the milk is produced from a pregnancy resulting from zina. The question: does such milk also create mahram relationships with the biological father (the adulterer) and his relatives?
3
State the two positions
First position (some Hanafis): milk from zina is like legitimate milk and prohibits marriage to the adulterer and his ascendants/descendants, based on partial lineage (shubhat al-juz'iyya). Second position (al-Wabiri, preferred in Fath al-Qadir): prohibition is only from the mother's side; from the father's side it requires established lineage (nasab).
The passage uses 'qil' (it is said) for the first view, indicating it is not the relied-upon view.
4
Analyze the proof structure
Both sides use qiyas. The first view analogizes to legitimate milk and the prohibition of a child born from zina (which is prohibited to the father). The second view analogizes to the child of zina: such a child is not prohibited to the father's relatives unless nasab is proven. The commentator sides with the second analogy.
The dalil is based on the principle that rada' creates mahram like lineage, but lineage from zina is incomplete without acknowledgment.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah
The preferred view is that milk from zina prohibits marriage to the mother and her relatives, but to the father only if paternity is legally established. The practical difference: without acknowledgment, the nursing child could marry the biological father's relatives (e.g., his son) but not the mother's son.
This ruling is found in the fatawa of the commentator and is supported by the author of Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزوجها عليهما عليه كالنسب، وفروعه، والزوجان عليهما ) : أي تحرم المرضعة وزوجها على الرّضيع ، ويحرم قومهما على الرضيع كما في النسب
[1] قوله : وزوجها فيه إشارة عدم حرمة الزاني عليه، وكذا أقربائه، وقـد اختلف فيه، فقيل : لبن الزنا كالحلال، فإذا أرضعت به بنتاً حرمت على الزاني وآبائه وأبنائه والعمّ الزاني وأخيه التزوّج بها، كالمولودة من الزنا ؛ فإنّها تحرم على الزاني وأصوله وفروعه بشبهة الجزئية، ولا تحرم على العم والأخ.
وذكر الوبري : إنّ الحرمة تثبت من جهة الأم خاصة، ما لم يثبت النسب فحينئذ تثبت من جهة الأب، ورجحه في «فتح القدير ) ، وقد بسطت الكلام في هذه المسألة في بعض فتاواي ردّاً على من نازعني فيها وأتى بما أتى.
And her husband on both of them upon him like lineage, and his descendants, and the two spouses on both of them): i.e., the nursing mother and her husband are prohibited to the nursing infant, and their relatives are prohibited to the nursing infant as in lineage. [1] His statement: 'and her husband' — in it is an indication of the non-prohibition of the adulterer upon him, and likewise his relatives. And there has been disagreement (ikhtilaf) about it. Some said: milk from zina is like permissible milk, so if a woman breastfeeds a girl with it, the girl becomes prohibited to the adulterer, his fathers, his sons, and the adulterer's paternal uncle, and his brother marrying her, like a child born from zina; for she is prohibited to the adulterer, his ascendants, and his descendants due to the semblance of juz'iyya (partial lineage), and she is not prohibited to the paternal uncle and brother. And al-Wabiri mentioned: that prohibition is established from the mother's side only, as long as lineage is not established; then when lineage is established, it is established from the father's side. And he (al-Wabiri) preferred this in 'Fath al-Qadir'. And I (the commentator) have expanded the discussion on this issue in some of my fatawa in response to those who disputed with me on it and came with what they came.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage comprises a ruling and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The ruling proper is that the wet nurse's husband (who provided the milk) is also prohibited to the nursing infant, along with his relatives, just as in lineage. This is based on the hadith that rada' makes mahram those who would be mahram by blood. The controversy arises over milk produced from an extramarital relationship (zinā). Two positions are presented: (1) Some hold that milk from zinā is like legitimate milk in creating prohibitions, extending to the biological father (the adulterer) and his ascendants/descendants, analogous to the prohibition of biological lineage in cases of zinā (partial lineage via resemblance). (2) Al-Wabiri's view, preferred in 'Fath al-Qadir', states that the prohibition is established only from the mother's side (i.e., the woman who gave birth and breastfed), not from the father, unless paternity is legally established (which is typically not the case for an adulterer). The commentator mentions he has written on this in his fatawa. The preferred position in the Hanafi school is that milk from zinā does establish prohibition from the mother's side, and from the father's side only if lineage is established. However, the passage shows authoritative figures engaged in taqliq (discussion), indicating that the issue is not completely settled.

Key Terms
لبن الزنا (laban al-zina): Milk produced as a result of a pregnancy from extramarital intercourse (zinā).
زوج المرضعة (zawj al-murdi'ah): The husband of the wet nurse, considered the 'father' of the milk child for prohibition purposes.
شبهة الجزئية (shubhat al-juz'iyya): The notion of partial lineage or semblance of parentage; in zina, the child shares partial biological connection to the father but not full legal lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view in this passage, does milk from zinā establish prohibition of marriage to the biological father (the adulterer)?
A) Yes, whether or not lineage is proven.
B) No, never.
C) Only if lineage is established (e.g., if he acknowledges the child).
D) Only for the father's ascendants, not descendants.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, milk from zina creates mahram status on the mother's side only unless the father's lineage is established.
